Complete Compilation of Ancient and Modern Books, Medical Section, Volume 388

Women in Labor

Huangdi's Suwen

Discussion on the Fetus

The Emperor said: How can one know that a woman is pregnant and about to give birth? Qibo replied: When the body is ill but there are no abnormal pulses. [Note: Qi governs the creation of life, while blood is responsible for formation. A pregnant woman has the harmony of blood and qi. "About to give birth" refers to how the harmony of blood and qi forms the fetus, which is temporarily lodged in the abdomen without the guidance of channels. Thus, at the term of ten months, it can become exhausted and come out. One must understand that menstruation during pregnancy is blood that resides in the qi division and not in the channels. If the body is ill, menstruation does not arrive. If there are no abnormal pulses, blood and qi are in harmony.][1p]

The Classic of Pulses (by Wang Shuhe, Jin Dynasty)

The Pulses of Pregnancy

When a woman is pregnant, her pulse is superficial. If there is abdominal pain radiating to the lower back, it indicates she is about to give birth. However, an irregular pulse does not indicate illness. Moreover, if a woman is about to give birth, her pulse will be irregular; she may awaken at midnight and give birth by noon.

The Thousand Gold Prescriptions (by Sun Simiao, Tang Dynasty)

Discussion on Difficulties in Childbirth

Though a woman in labor may be seen as unclean, during the time of pain and whether before or after childbirth, her family members should not be allowed to view her, as it may cause complications. If she has already given birth, it can harm the child. When a woman is about to give birth, it is especially important to avoid having too many people watching; only two or three individuals should be nearby. Once the labor is over, then she can inform others. If there are many people watching, it will lead to a difficult delivery.

For all childbirth, one should not be hasty or fearful; those around her must remain calm and composed. They should avoid causing any anxiety or distress, as worry will hinder delivery. If she experiences abdominal pain and feels heat in her eyes, it indicates that the child has not yet turned for birth. After the child is born, everyone, including the mother, should avoid asking whether it is a boy or a girl, and the mother should not be allowed to see anything unclean.[2p]
Women's Good Practices
[Song Dynasty, Chen Ziming]

On Protecting Pregnant Women

Whenever a woman is pregnant until her due month, she should calm her mind and settle her worries, walk regularly, and avoid excessive sleeping and eating. She should refrain from drinking alcoholic beverages and consuming mixed medicines. It is advisable to first affix the birth chart, properly arrange the bedding and curtains, and prepare experienced midwives along with the necessary herbs and utensils. When labor begins, it is crucial to avoid noisy crowds and panic; only two elderly women should assist her to walk and support her while standing. If she feels a discharge of fluid and experiences severe pain in her waist and abdomen, it indicates the fetus is misaligned. The mother should lie on her back to encourage the baby to turn, with the head positioned towards the birth canal, and use medications to expedite labor. If she feels anxious, a spoonful of white honey mixed with water can be taken. If she feels hungry, a small amount of porridge should be consumed. She must not be allowed to feel excessive hunger or thirst, as it may weaken her strength. Do not administer labor-inducing medicines too early; this should be approached with caution.

Lunar Calendar Directions

January, March, May, July, September, and November are associated with Bing and Ren.
February, April, June, August, October, and December are associated with Jia and Geng.[3p]
Guide to Placing Birth Supplies and Clothing in Favorable Directions During the Month

When arranging positions for birth supplies and clothing, one should distribute them within the sleeping chamber. According to the "Tai Ping Sheng Hui Fang," when a pregnant woman first enters her confinement period, she should create a birth chart, writing the specific month and day in red ink, and hang it in an appropriate location. For example, if the month is January and it corresponds to the positions of Bing and Ren, the birthing bed and canopy should be placed in the Ren position; the clothing should be stored in the Bing position, with the chart affixed to the north wall of the birthing room. If there is a leap month, one should rely on the seasonal divisions.

Moreover, each month’s birth chart includes the deities: Lei Gong, Zhao Yao, Yun Gui, Tian Gou, Xuan Yuan, Da Shi, Xian Chi, Feng Long, Wu Shi, Bai Hu, Da Fu, Tian Hou, and Kuang Hu, totaling thirteen spirits, each assigned positions according to the lunar cycles. The term "Yue Kong" refers to the empty space in the lunar orb, and Wang Bing’s commentary states that it indicates the absence of the moon’s light, thus not counting among the thirteen spirits.

Now, "Tai Ping Sheng Hui Fang" indicates that during the six yang months, the position is at Bing and Ren, while the six yin months are placed at Jia and Geng. This is consistent with what "Wai Tai" mentions, where January aligns with Bing and Ren and December with Jia and Geng, and the reasoning is the same. However, "Wai Tai" elaborates while "Sheng Hui" is concise, and people today often prefer the simpler version.

Some say that when arranging birth supplies and clothing each month, one should orient them towards the directions of lunar merit and lunar emptiness, with all thirteen deities and spirits being adjusted according to the seasonal changes. If transitioning to the next month’s seasonal division, one should not use the chart from the previous month.[4p]
If the 14th day of the first month is the start of spring, a pregnant woman should rest for thirteen days and not use the previous year's methods. One must follow the lunar phase for guidance. If one uses the seasonal indicators instead, the heavenly and lunar virtues will be misaligned. However, the concept of "empty sky" and its associated meanings are somewhat similar in this context. Some argue that "sky" does not pertain to the thirteen deities, as the chart includes Tian Yi, a noble position that has no peer; thus, this emptiness is considered "sky." During this time, it is not suitable for anything but to prepare the birthing bed and store clothes.

The "Jisheng Calendar" states: The celestial virtue in the first month is associated with Ding, in the second month with Kun, in the third month with Ren, in the fourth month with Xin, in the fifth month with Gan, in the sixth month with Jia, in the seventh month with Gui, in the eighth month with Gen, in the ninth month with Bing, in the tenth month with Yi, in the eleventh month with Xun, and in the twelfth month with Tian.

Furthermore, the "Kanyu Calendar" mentions the traveling year, the White Tiger, and the killing deities positioned one hour after the Tai Sui. For instance, if Tai Sui is in Mao, then the White Tiger is in Yin, following similarly for others. If childbirth occurs or clothes are stored when these are violated, it will bring misfortune to both mother and child.

Wang Ziheng states in the "Discussion on Difficult Births": It posits that violating any of the deities set forth is a logical consideration. However, there are also cases of natural difficult births, where the child is born in a reverse position, or when the intestines descend, which may resume normalcy after delivery. This is not caused by illness. The dynamics of Qi and blood govern these matters; there are principles in the world that cannot be extensively questioned, and one should be aware of them.

Safe childbirth and the auspicious positioning of clothes among the thirteen deities indicate good and bad omens. Refer to the diagram.[5p]

Methods for Women in Childbirth

Nurturing Direction: The birthing woman should sit and lie down facing this direction, with the door of the birthing tent opened towards it, which is very auspicious.

Reversal Month: In this month, spread ashes, using either cowhide or donkey skin underneath, then spread grass on top. Do not let any foul blood soil the ground; this is auspicious.

Disaster Month: One should not give birth in this period and should not relieve themselves in this direction; avoid it for great auspiciousness.

Life and Death Direction: One should not give birth in this direction and should not relieve themselves, either small or large; avoiding this direction is greatly auspicious.

Hanging Corpses Day: On this day, do not climb ropes. It is advisable to hang a horse rein and use that to climb; this is very auspicious.

Closed Stomach Direction: During the month of giving birth and through the full moon, one should not relieve themselves in this direction or discard impure water; caution here brings good fortune.

Eight Anus Direction: The birthing tent should not have its door opening towards this direction; it is to be avoided for great auspiciousness.

Borrowing the Earth Method of Ti Yuanzi

Borrow ten steps to the east, borrow ten steps to the west, borrow ten steps to the south, borrow ten steps to the north, borrow ten steps above, borrow ten steps below. Within the walls, more than forty steps, secure the borrowed land. There may be impurities, or the Eastern Sea God, or the Western Sea God, or the Southern Sea God, or the Northern Sea God, or the Sun General and the Lady White Tiger; go away ten zhang. Xuanyuan and Zhao Yao rise high by ten zhang. The heavenly talisman and earth axis sink into the ground by ten zhang. Make the land vacant, so that Ms. Mu can reside peacefully without obstacles, without fear or dread, supported by all deities, and let all evils swiftly depart. Urgently, as per the decree, command.

[The above borrowing method should be written in red on the first day of the entering month and affixed to the wall of the birthing chamber, without needing to avoid any deities or malevolent influences.][9p]
Prohibition on Grass

When laying down grass and felt mats, one should chant: "Iron, iron, broth, not to be used by the public." The king receives from this one word of copper, one word of iron, as mother and child give birth to each other, all disregarding iron. Urgent, urgent, as per the law's command.

Prohibition on Water

When storing water for childbirth, one should chant: "Homage to the Three Treasures Water." Water in the well is well water, water in the river is river water, water in the vessel is pure water, water in the law is true water. Know well that it is not true; do not treat it as true water. Hold purity over turbidity, govern the upright over the wicked. Sun travels, moon kills, five warriors, generals, azure dragon, white tiger, vermilion bird, original martial, wandering, celestial dog, Xuanyuan, female prostitute, heaven devours, earth devours, hanging moon, closed womb, six virtues forbidden, twelve divine kings, earth charms immobilizing spirits; each must stay in their place, without movement or disturbance; do not offend or interfere. If there is any movement, if there is any interference, apply the divine incantation, and your form shall be restrained. Acha ni A Kun luo mo duo li su di li su he.[10p]
To manage childbirth is challenging; facing adverse conditions, one must ensure the vital essence is retained.

On Difficult Childbirth

Women primarily rely on blood, and when the qi is smooth, the blood harmonizes, leading to a safe delivery. However, in wealthy households, excessive comfort can cause qi stagnation, preventing the fetus from moving, or sometimes the mingling of essence and blood in the womb leads to childbirth difficulties. If the abdomen hurts intermittently, it is called "playing with the fetus," and if the midwife is unaware and examines the water, it can lead to the rupture of membranes and dryness, making it difficult for the child to turn or be born. Generally, childbirth should occur when contractions are extreme and the child is pressing against the birth canal; only then is it appropriate to sit on grass. In the heat of summer, if there is an outpouring of blood, it’s important to drink clear water to resolve it. At the end of winter and the beginning of spring, warmth should be provided to the lower part of the birthing room with fire, and the clothing must be thick and warm to prevent the fetus from being chilled. Bathing the head and washing the feet in the last month may also cause childbirth difficulties.

Note: If the membranes rupture early and the blood and water dry up, resulting in labor exhaustion affecting the qi and blood, decocting Eight Treasures Decoction or Complete Nourishing Decoction with additional Motherwort and taking it occasionally can provide support. Alternatively, using several pounds of Astragalus, and around four to five pounds of Angelica and Chuanxiong, boiled in a large pot of water can fill the room with medicinal vapor to benefit the mother. The umbilical cord should be burnt with oil paper for cauterization to restore the vital energy. Midwives must be experienced and should first provide assistance while informing the patient. If labor progresses slowly, simply say it's not yet time; if it’s a twin pregnancy, indicate that the afterbirth hasn't yet been expelled. Fear can disperse the qi, making it even more difficult for the labor to be successful.[12p]
On Difficult Labor by Guo Jizhong

Difficult labor occurs when the fetus is not positioned correctly, causing the head to rest on blood clots, which, along with stagnant blood within the womb, obstructs the ease of delivery. As a result, the labor becomes difficult, and one should urgently administer Shengjin Powder to disperse the blood, facilitating the baby’s birth. Chen Wuze states that this often happens when the fetus has not turned properly, when the mother begins labor too early, or when excessive effort is made, resulting in the rupture of the amniotic sac and the drying up of blood and fluids. This can lead to a constricted birth canal, making the descent difficult for the baby. It is advisable to first take a labor-inducing remedy like Shen San to stabilize the blood. If there is a transverse or breech presentation, one should apply acupuncture according to established methods.[13p]

Yangzi's Treatise on Childbirth

In all matters of childbirth, one must first understand these ten principles to avoid jeopardizing the lives of both mother and child through unjust causes. In the world, those who assist in births often lack skillful hands, leading to numerous deaths. Hence, I speak from experience and pain.

  1. The first is proper childbirth. A woman carries a child for ten months, with sufficient yin and yang energy. If suddenly there are intense pains in the waist and abdomen, and the fetal energy descends, leading to extreme pain in the navel and abdomen, followed by severe pain in the waist, and the water breaks and blood flows, then the child is born; this is called proper childbirth.

  2. The second is obstructed childbirth. A person’s life is determined by the balance of yin and yang, each having its own time that cannot be altered. If, before childbirth has progressed for a month, the woman suddenly experiences abdominal pain as if she is about to give birth but nothing happens, this is called trial labor, not proper childbirth.

In all cases, if the mother has not reached the signs of proper childbirth, one should not support her by holding her waist, nor should the mother recklessly exert force. For a woman who wishes to give birth, if there is abdominal pain but the baby is not in position, the assisting midwife may advise the mother to exert herself. If the baby merely shifts slightly and the mother exerts excessive pressure, it may cause the baby to become misaligned or turned incorrectly, preventing a proper birth—all of which are results of inappropriate force applied by the midwife.

For any mother giving birth, one must wait until the child is correctly positioned to begin pushing at the moment of delivery; this is the appropriate time for the mother to exert herself.[14p]
If the signs of a proper delivery have not yet appeared and one exerts effort too early, recklessly takes medicine, or causes any disturbance, it may result in the child being born prematurely. This is akin to pulling seedlings to hasten their growth, which is of no benefit and can be harmful. This is called injuring the delivery.

The third is called inducing labor. When a woman is about to give birth, with her waters breaking and blood flowing, she experiences severe abdominal pain, a heavy feeling in her waist, and her head is already visible at the birth canal; these are the signs of a proper delivery. If, however, the child does not arrive, it is appropriate to take medicine to induce the birth. Even if several days have passed and the mother experiences intense discomfort while the signs of a proper delivery are evident, if the child is still difficult to deliver, it is also permissible to take medicine to support the mother's vital energy and expedite the child's birth. This is called inducing labor.

The fourth is called obstructed delivery. In the cold winter months, if the mother's menstrual blood becomes cold and congeals, it can prevent the child from being born, which is very detrimental. A woman giving birth in winter should not remove her warm clothing from her lower body and should avoid sitting or lying in cold places. The room should be kept warm with a fire, allowing the mother to face the warmth while ensuring her lower abdomen and knees remain warm. If the blood warms up, it will flow easily, facilitating the child's birth. This is called obstructed delivery.

The fifth is called heated delivery. In the hot summer months, the mother needs to maintain a suitable temperature; she should not excessively seek coolness, which can damage the vital energy of the fetus. Crowding is also to be avoided, as the heat may overwhelm the mother, causing her blood to boil and leading to symptoms like fever, headache, flushed face, and disorientation, to the point where she may not recognize those around her. This is called heated delivery. Even in cool windy or rainy summer weather, one should not seek excessive coolness, as it could lead to serious illness.

The sixth is called transverse delivery.[15p]
If the child's hand or arm comes out first, this is due to the mother exerting herself improperly before the appropriate time. If the child's body is not positioned correctly and there is a forceful push, it can result in the body being crossed and unable to be born. The mother should be comfortably lying on her back, and then the attendant should first push the hand, guiding it up straight so that the head aligns with the birth canal. Gradually encourage the body down, using the middle finger to massage the shoulder without constraining the umbilical cord, guiding it upwards and correcting it, or using a finger to grasp the ear for correction. The mother must be lying on her back as you guide the child upwards slowly and steadily. When the body is aligned, give her a prepared herbal decoction, and only then can she begin to push for the child to be born. This is known as transverse presentation.

The seventh situation is called breech presentation. When the mother lacks sufficient energy and the contractions are not strong, pushing too soon can prevent the child from turning, causing the feet to come out first. The mother should lie on her back, and the attendant should gently push the feet back in. The mother must not exert any effort whatsoever, nor should there be any panic, allowing the child to position itself naturally.

The eighth situation is known as oblique presentation. If the child is not properly aligned and the mother pushes, the head can get lodged against the left or right leg, making it unable to descend even if the head is visible. The mother should lie on her back, and the attendant should gently push the child upward, using their hands to align the head properly. Once the head is correctly positioned, the mother can then push to give birth.[16p]
If the infant's head is tilted backward and only the forehead is exposed, the attending person should use a soft fabric to warm and cradle the head gently, then lightly push the infant's head to align it correctly. The mother should be instructed to exert her effort to assist in the delivery. This situation is called "tilted birth."

The ninth situation is called "obstructed birth." If the infant's body is positioned correctly, with the top of the head visible but unable to emerge, it may be due to the body twisting, causing the abdomen to compress the shoulders. In this case, the mother should lie on her back, and the attending person should gently push the infant upward while gradually guiding with the hand. Using the middle finger, apply pressure below the infant's shoulder to adjust the abdomen, ensuring the infant's body is aligned before the mother exerts her effort to deliver the child. This is referred to as "obstructed birth."

The tenth situation is called "sitting birth."[17p]
When a child is about to be born, if the mother is fatigued and has been sitting for a long time leaning against a mattress, obstructing the birth path, she should urgently tie a handkerchief to a high point and hold onto it with her hand, gently bending her legs and sitting down to facilitate the child's birth, without sitting on any object. This is called sitting birth.

The eleventh method is called "coiled intestines birth." When giving birth, the mother's intestines come out first before the child, and the intestines do not retract. Mix half a cup of vinegar with half a cup of freshly drawn water and apply it to the face of the birthing mother. With each application, the intestines retract; after three applications, they should retract completely. This is an effective method.

Note: According to ancient methods, 49 seeds of hemp should be ground and applied to the top of the birthing mother’s head to help retract the intestines, which should then be washed off quickly. If the intestines are out, use a small amount of moistened grinding knife water, warmed slightly over a fire, and drink a decoction made with magnetite, which should help in retracting them. The magnetite must be verified for use by yin-yang practitioners. If water is applied to the mother’s face, it may frighten her, causing her energy to disperse.[18p]
Translation:

Joint bones not opening and birth doors not closing

It is my humble opinion that when the joint bones do not open and the birth doors do not close, it is due to the fundamental energy being weak. Before childbirth, if there is a failure to regulate and nurture, the flow of Qi and blood cannot circulate properly. For joint bones not opening, indicating deficiency of Yin Qi, use the modified Xiang Gui Decoction and the Bai Zhong Yi Qi Decoction. For birth doors not closing, indicating deficiency of Qi and blood, use the Shi Quan Da Bu Decoction.

Childbirth difficulty and death of the fetus in the womb

The difficulty in childbirth and the death of the fetus in the womb often arise from being startled too early or violating prohibitions, leading to an early loss of blood and the drying out of the fetus. One must examine the mother; if her tongue is dark blue, the fetus is dead. Therefore, in the childbirth chamber, sitting and lying must align with the directions of the four seasons and adhere to the five elements to avoid taboos for good fortune.

Note: The death of the fetus in the womb often results from being startled too early, violating prohibitions, carrying heavy loads, or frequent probing to check for amniotic fluid, causing the membranes to rupture and blood and fluid to deplete, resulting in fetal desiccation. If the mother’s lips and tongue are dark, both mother and child are dead. If the tongue is blue or there is significant swelling and tightness, the fetus is already dead. First, take one ounce of Ping Wei San with half an ounce of wine and water, decoct it, and then add half an ounce of saltpetre, or use one ounce of saltpetre with children's urine to mix and administer, which works wonders.[19p]
When a fetus dies in the womb due to a fever

If a fever causes a fetus to die and cannot be expelled, taking Heishensan will allow the fetus to descend naturally.

Note: According to Mr. Chen Wuze, the symptoms should first be examined in the mother. If the face is red and the tongue is blue, it indicates the child has died; if the face is blue and the tongue is red, it suggests the mother has died while the child survives; if the lips are blue and there is foaming at the mouth, it means both mother and child have died. In the case of twins, one may live while the other dies. Heishensan is thought to be too hot and should not be used lightly; in cases where one fetus is already dead, it is safer to use Pingweisan, with shibuxiao and mercury to assist in expulsion, which minimizes harm to the living fetus. Furthermore, Guo states that when the mother suffers from a fever for six to seven days, the heat severely cooks the fetus, leading to its death. The deceased child is cold and cannot be expelled on its own, but by taking Heishensan to warm the fetus, it will soon warm up and be expelled naturally.[20p]
Afterbirth Not Expelling

Guo Jizhong said: If the afterbirth does not come down, it is because the woman is exhausted and cannot push it out. Sometimes blood may enter the sac, causing it to swell and preventing it from descending, which leads to a feeling of fullness and pain in the chest, along with rapid breathing. Quickly take the Dueling Life Pill to disperse the blood and reduce the swelling, and the afterbirth will descend by itself. The Niuxi Powder is also effective.

Note: If the intestines are coming out and there is a deficiency of qi preventing them from retracting, use the Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction, or grind one ounce of flaxseed and apply it to the top of the mother’s head. If the afterbirth does not descend, apply flaxseed to the heart of the right foot; when the afterbirth comes down, wash it immediately. If delayed, the afterbirth may remain inside. The Yi Mu Pill is also effective.

If the afterbirth has not descended and you wish to cut the umbilical cord, you must first tie a small object to weigh it down before cutting it; otherwise, the placenta may cause sudden death. If lochia is flowing within the sac and causes abdominal fullness and pain, take the Dueling Life Pill or the Shixiao Powder to dissolve the stagnant blood; if delayed, it may not be salvaged. If the vital energy cannot mobilize, and there is no abdominal fullness or pain, use the Bao Sheng Wu You Powder to replenish and stabilize the vital energy. Apply flaxseed flesh to the heart of the mother's right foot, and when the afterbirth descends, wash it away; if delayed, the intestines may also come out. If the intestines do not retract, use this ointment applied to the crown of the head, and the intestines will retract by themselves.

Note: Guo also mentions that at times, after the initial descent of the fetus, the mother may be weak and unable to exert more energy, leading to a halt in the expulsion of the placenta. If cold wind acts upon her, the blood vessels may become blocked, preventing the afterbirth from descending. In such a case, take one handful of black beans, fry them until well-cooked, mix with a cup of vinegar, boil for three to five times, strain, and divide into three doses to be taken warm.[21p]
Difficulties of Labor Pulse Manual

For women in labor, the pulse is mixed with the channels.
[Note: In the "Nanjing": One breath with three pulses is called "off-channel"; this means the Yang is doubled compared to Yin. One breath with one pulse is also called "off-channel"; this means Yin is quadrupled compared to Yang. The note states: "Channel" refers to the constant state; the stomach pulse deviates from its regular measure. In healthy individuals, one breath results in two pulses, and one inhale also results in two pulses, hence it is called the pulse of harmony. Therefore, with one breath, the pulse travels three inches, and with one inhale, it travels three inches; when breathing stabilizes, the pulse travels six inches. In one day and night, there are thirteen thousand five hundred breaths, making the pulse travel eight hundred ten zhang, indicating one cycle, returning to the original channel once more. Now, with one breath, the pulse reaches three pulses, and with one inhale, three pulses are also noted. When breathing stabilizes, the pulse travels nine inches. If there is one breath with one pulse, the pulse travels one and a half inches; one inhale with one pulse travels one and a half inches; when breathing stabilizes, the pulse travels three inches, resulting in a total of four hundred single zhang in one day and night, referred to as one cycle; this is less than the count of a normal pulse. Thus, it cycles and repeats, also not returning to the original channel, and is likewise termed "off-channel."] It is described as deep, fine, and slippery.[22p]

Jisheng Fang
(Song Dynasty - Yan Yonghe)

Discussion on Reducing a Fat Fetus

After ten months of pregnancy, the body completes its development. At this point, one should begin to take medicines to reduce a fat fetus for easier delivery. In modern times, many people resort to the use of bitter orange powder. This is not without reason, but if the fetal energy is already robust, it is suitable for consumption. Moreover, both bitter orange and big belly peel can help reduce the fetus; however, if the fetal energy is inherently weak, why should it be further diminished? It is better to use the "Rescue Life Powder" to stabilize the fetus and nourish its energy, making the baby small and healthy for an easier birth, ensuring a more secure delivery.

Transverse Presentation at Birth

All cases of transverse presentation are due to a failure to restrict one's diet and overindulgence in food, leading to stagnation in the five organs and disharmony in the six bowels. When the fetal energy is already robust, exerting too early or frightening the fetus can lead to complications. An urgent use of the "Golden Liquid for Reducing the Fetus" can help ensure the child is born smoothly.

Feeling Distressed Before Birth

If one suddenly feels a blockage in the circulating blood and energy, losing consciousness, it is likely due to excessive exertion, leading to weak pulse dynamics, mental fatigue, a feeling of pressure in the chest, closed eyes, and stifled mouth—with a pale face and rigidity. Vitality may be at risk, and in such cases, "Lifesaving Powder" should be used urgently.

Difficulty in Delivering a Fat Fetus

Why is it difficult to deliver a fat fetus? Those in wealth and nobility often despise bland foods, indulging in rich, fatty delicacies without moderation, eating to satiation before resting, which leads to thickening of the fetal sac and a firm attachment. This urgent energy during movement is because they have not prepared by taking medicines to reduce the fat fetus. Consequently, when the time for delivery arrives, it is certain to be difficult. One may take "Wuyou Powder" in the last month to facilitate an easier birth.[25p]
Sitting on Grass

When one suddenly suffers from impotence while seated on grass, with eyes rolling and mouth sealed, what can be the cause? It is due to indulging in unchecked joys and anger, which leads to the exhaustion of vitality and the decline of health. The fetus becomes hard to move; sitting on grass excessively can cause abdominal pain that cannot be tolerated, leading to rolling eyes, a sealed mouth, a dark face, blue lips, and foam at the mouth. Both mother and child may perish. If the mother shows a slight flush while the child dies, one should urgently administer the Thunderbolt Life-Taking Pill for rescue.

General Discussion

When the child dies in the womb and blood violently descends, with the womb being unable to deliver, one should take Banxia Decoction. If the fetus is dead but not expelled, one should take the San Yi Chengqi Decoction. The issue arises from wind-heat drying and constricting, causing the birth passage to not open naturally. Symptoms include a reversed pulse, a taut pulse, a red or blue face, or a change in color to five hues, with abdominal fullness, urgent pain, and difficulty breathing—indicating that the fetus is no longer moving. If the hands and feet are warm and the pulse is slippery, it indicates a difficult birth, but one should promote and smooth the labor without forcing delivery. In cases where the fetus is dead and not expelled, take the San Yi Chengqi Decoction followed by a dose of the Yiyuan Powder. After a short while, frequently use oil and paste to mix with Yiyuan Powder and take warm. If both are expelled, the mother may survive. Difficult births or retained dead fetuses occur from wind-heat drying and constricted accumulation, preventing softening; thus, labor does not occur naturally. This medicine's potency can frequently relieve the accumulation and facilitate delivery. Afterward, care should be taken to avoid warming and replenishing to prevent the resurgence of dryness and heat.[26p]

Danxi's Heart Method
Yuan Dynasty, Zhu Zhenheng

Treatment Method

Difficult labor is caused by deficiency in qi and blood. This often occurs when one does not take precautions during the months of September and October. There can also be stagnation of qi and blood preventing movement. In the month of labor, one should use wild tianma to brew a paste, and mix it with white soup. Combine thoroughly with oil and honey, adjusting with urine until perfectly blended.[27p]
Pulse Diagnosis Method

In general, if a pregnant woman's pulse is fine and even, she will have an easy labor. If it is strong and floating, with scattered heat, it will be difficult to give birth.

Stillbirth Examination Method

If the fetus dies in the womb, the mother will have a pale face, blue nails, blue lips and tongue, and a foul mouth odor. If both cheeks are slightly red, the mother is alive but the child is dead.

Discussion on Difficult Labor (by Zhu Zhenheng, Yuan Dynasty)

Difficult labor often occurs in those who are depressed and indulged, in wealthy and pampered families, while the poor and hardworking do not experience it. The medical texts only mention a formula for thin fetuses, created for Princess Huyang, which is not the ultimate truth. Why is this? When seeing those who use this formula, their difficulties seem to resolve. My sister suffered from difficult labor; later, when she was pregnant, she experienced a setback. I felt great pity. Observing her body as plump but inactive with needles, I contemplated for days and suddenly realized: this is the opposite of Princess Huyang's case. Those who are pampered have strong qi, while exhausting their qi leads to peace, hence easy childbirth. Now, with her plump body suggesting weak qi, long sitting indicating stagnation, her qi weakens further, and the fetus cannot move due to the mother's weak qi. By nourishing the mother's qi, her body becomes healthy and labor is made easy. When she was five or six months pregnant, I applied a formula for qi supplement and a dozen patches along with the major formula Zisu, resulting in a quick delivery of a boy. Thereafter, I further adjusted this formula based on the mother's condition, color, temperament, and seasonal changes, with every adjustment yielding results. Thus, I named this formula "Great Achievement Birth Powder."[28p]
Medical Guidelines by Lou Ying (Ming Dynasty)

On Yang Zijiang's Method for Handling Abortion

Yang Zijiang's discussion on abortion methods contains crucial insights that must not be taken lightly. If, before the full term of ten months, there are abdominal pains that come and go or are mild, it is termed 'misplaced pain,' and does not indicate proper labor. If abdominal pain is severe but the lower back is not, it does not indicate proper labor. If the fetus has not yet descended, it does not indicate proper labor. If there is no thrusting or bulging in the birth canal, it does not indicate proper labor. If the amniotic fluid has not broken and blood has not come out, it does not indicate proper labor. If there is bleeding but no abdominal pain, it does not indicate proper labor. In the absence of signs of proper labor, assist the woman to walk gently or support her when she cannot walk. She may sit, rest, or take one or two doses of calming medication, then stop. Be cautious not to recklessly administer labor-inducing medicines, as this may cause anxiety in the mother and diminish her resolve.[29p]
It is essential to ensure that the mother is at ease, nurturing her body and mind, and for the midwife to first provide her with guidance. If she feels anxious and troubled, she can take a spoonful of white honey and dissolve it in newly drawn water. Care must be taken not to exert unnecessary force, as this could distress the mother. Only when the child presses against the birth canal, causing extreme pain in the lower back and a fiery sensation in the eyes, is it appropriate to exert effort and take labor-inducing medicine.

One man’s wife experienced severe pain in her lower back and abdomen as if she were about to give birth, with her discomfort intensifying significantly, only slightly alleviated during certain hours. This continued for over ten days without any signs of delivery. Upon reviewing this guidance, she was given pregnancy-preserving medicine with addition of ginseng and atractylodes, along with nourishing foods, leading to her stabilization and relief from pain. More than twenty days later, she finally gave birth to a son. Had she moved recklessly or used force during that time, or taken labor-inducing medicines prematurely, it would have led to grave danger.[30p]
On the Four Methods of Difficult Delivery in Yang Zijiang's Theory

In Yang Zijiang's ten methods of delivery, there are four categories: 横产 (Cross Delivery), 偏产 (Oblique Delivery), 碍产 (Obstructed Delivery), and 倒产 (Reversed Delivery). If one observes the situation of the mother giving birth, one must not rely on these methods unless one is a skilled and proficient practitioner, lest ignorance lead to harm. The reversed delivery refers to cases where the child is often born with its feet first, and there is no subsequent issue, as both mother and child are intact; there is no need to adhere strictly to the methods implied for head-first delivery. In obstructed delivery, the umbilical cord may be wrapped around the top of the child’s head while the child’s head itself emerges from the birth canal; a practitioner may use their hands to guide the cord down from the child’s head. If the cord is loosely wrapped once around the head, and the child along with the placenta naturally descends, there is no complication, and it is not necessary to use methods for obstructed delivery.

Difficult Delivery Explanation

The Inner Canon states: If the breath does not circulate, the flow is exhausted; if there is no continuity even for a moment, the foundation collapses. The circulation of qi and blood must flow continuously; a lack thereof endangers the body. If a pregnant woman has the child in her womb, the mother and child share a flow of energy, entirely relying on nourishment. After ten months, the blood and qi are full, and both form and spirit are complete; suddenly, as if waking from a dream, she can use her hands to break the amniotic sac and find a path to delivery. Once outside the sac, with mother and child separate, their breathing may differ; they cannot remain blocked internally for long, leading to stunted circulation. For a robust fetus, once the sac is broken, it naturally follows the fluid down easily, resulting in an uncomplicated delivery.[31p]
The weak and troubled ones turn their heads slowly; the amniotic fluid has dried up, and foul blood obstructs the path, causing stagnation. Thus, a miscarriage occurs, and the unborn child dies in the womb, leading to the mother’s death in an instant. Should this not be feared? Whenever anticipating birth, if the amniotic fluid has already discharged and time passes without delivery, one should deliberate and plan, using medicines to expel the bad blood, ensuring the path for the child is clear to prevent difficulties in labor. How can one simply wait idly for death? Therefore, the medicines for inducing labor—such as Chuanxiong, Angelica, Motherwort, and Malva seeds—are all meant to expel the foul blood. If the lower back and abdomen do not hurt excessively, and the fluid drips down, it is known as "trial fluid," not true amniotic fluid. One should maintain a calm mind and wait patiently, not hastily allowing a midwife to intervene. If the mother exerts too much force to deliver the child too early, it often leads to complications; thus, one must be cautious. If the hands or feet of the child are not positioned correctly, or the forehead is slightly exposed, one should gently adjust it by hand, waiting for it to descend naturally. Difficult labor occurs due to the mother’s indulgence prior to delivery. Not only difficult delivery but also various postnatal ailments arise from this.

When asked about the women described by Danxi, who find childbirth difficult after eight or nine months without restraint, the answer is that when desires stir, the vital energy and blood are depleted. The development of the fetus relies entirely on the nourishment of vital energy and blood. When vital energy and blood are deficient, the fetus weakens. After the amniotic fluid ruptures, it cannot turn and descend with the fluid, leading to difficulty in childbirth.[32p]
Introduction to Medicine
(Ming Dynasty, Li Cheng)

General Discussion

In October, when the Qi is abundant and the fetus is strong, if sudden abdominal pain occurs, or perhaps only back pain, and within moments labor begins, there is no need for urging; this is the natural occurrence of childbirth. It is advisable to take a single dose of nourishing mother paste to avoid postpartum complications. If there are individuals who are weak and anxious, experiencing intermittent abdominal pain, it is referred to as playful pain; if there is a trickle of fluid, it is known as testing water. Even if there is pain in both the abdomen and the navel, while the labor is vigorous and the waist is not painful, one must not be hasty. It is crucial to refrain from pressing on the abdomen or manipulating it, and simply wait until the time is right, when the abdominal pain intensifies and the water breaks, accompanied by back pain that feels like fire in the eyes, before sitting down to deliver. One must wait for the child’s head to descend properly and approach the birth canal before exerting force to deliver. If one sits down too early or exerts excessive force, it leads to maternal exhaustion and delays, necessitating the use of labor-inducing medicine.[33p]
All difficult births are caused by the expectant mother indulging in desires and being overly proud, leading to a lack of movement and consumption of raw, cold, and hard foods which cause stagnation. Some may have narrow pelvic bones; others may have a greatly enlarged abdomen with amniotic fluid not yet expelled; or if the presence of onlookers frightens the laboring woman, it can lead to a weakening of her spirit. When the spirit is weakened, the upper body becomes closed, and energy cannot flow downwards, causing distension and obstruction; in such cases, a sip of perilla leaf drink is most effective. For those with strong energy, use the weight-reducing sweet mixture; for those with weak energy, employ the labor-promoting decoction.

If abdominal pain occurs and the amniotic sac has not ruptured, one should use the ancient chuanxiong and angelica decoction to invigorate the blood. If the water sac has broken but there is only slight pain, or if there is pain without rhythmic contractions, one should take the calming fetus drink or the labor-promoting decoction to stabilize the fetal essence. One must not carelessly use strong medicines, as this could harm the water pathway and injure the fetus' energy, making the labor more difficult. The mother can listen to her own needs for sleep and food, but should not overindulge in sleep or food.

If there is excessive amniotic fluid, the blood will become desiccated. In this case, the ancient black divine powder must be used. If there is blood deficiency, the ancient chuanxiong and angelica decoction should be administered, known as the black divine powder; if there is weak energy, the four gentlemen decoction should be given, known as the four gentlemen's black divine powder. For transverse or breech presentations, add a pinch of musk. At this point, it is like a boat sitting on sand; one must bring in water before it can be cleared.[34p]
After taking this medicine, apply two jin of mashed scallions to the lower abdomen. Heat a dou of sand from a water's edge and place it over the scallions, gently rubbing it. If labor is slow despite the onset, it may be hindered by external wind, cold, or temperature changes. In summer, as heat causes energy to disperse and blood to boil, it is suitable to use Five Ling Powder with kuxingren. Alternatively, Three Retreats Six One Powder may be used. In winter, if there is freezing that leads to blood stagnation, the promotion of labor with Five Accumulations Powder is recommended.

If there is difficulty in passage and the waterway is dry, or if one has taken black Shen-tu (a type of medicine) and the effects are pronounced, use equal parts of clear oil and white honey, blended with broth from pig liver. Alternatively, take six one powder with seven qian and five qian of kuxingren, taken hot in doses of two qian each.

If there is prolonged difficulty in labor resulting in dry water and there is distress from evil influences, use Rabbit Brain Pill. For waist pain and anxiety, mix two qian each of ginseng and frankincense, and five fen of mercury to a powder, adjusting with egg white and diluting with ginger juice, taking it cold.

For transverse presentation, it is advisable to take Xiong Gui Black Shen Powder to solidify and promote blood production.[35p]
One must wait for the child to be positioned correctly and naturally at the door before taking powdered Ejiao, Talcum, and sunflower seeds mixed with warm wine and honey. Then apply force to assist the delivery.

In cases of difficult labor, it is best to lie calmly on the back. The midwife should gently push the feet inward and administer the Xiong Gui Heishen powder to secure and invigorate the blood while waiting for the child to descend properly. If there is a long delay with no progress, the midwife should gently use her hands to guide the feet upwards while ensuring the head gradually moves down. Continue taking Xiong Gui and other medicines until the child turns and is in the correct position, then use the San Tui powder mixed for assistance before applying force to aid the delivery. During labor, one should take blood-tonifying medicine.

For a situation where the intestines emerge first, quickly soak old cloths in hot water to soften them and cover the intestines, but do not wrap them entirely. Externally apply half a cup of vinegar mixed with seven parts fresh water and wash the mother’s face with it, ensuring it is fully absorbed. Also, apply Sheng Gao on the mother’s crown, wiping the intestines immediately. Internally take nourishing herbs like Xiong, Gui, Ginseng, and Astragalus, along with Ascending Hemp and Fang Feng for support, and success is always achieved.

In cases of obstructed labor, it is essential to take blood-tonifying medicine.[36p]
For lateral childbirth, it is advisable to take more of the Xiong Gui He Shen Powder.

If strong stimulating herbs are mistakenly used during labor, it can damage the mother's vital energy and blood. It is urgent to use calming remedies. After a period, labor will commence. Those who give birth on the first day, second to fourth days, or fifth day are all due to hurried and excessive exertion. Sometimes this is because the child wishes to be born, and when the baby's head breaks first, rot and blood may envelop it. It is recommended to use one ounce of salt and fermented soybean, wrapped in blue cloth and burned to maintain its properties, then mix one small quantity of musk into a powder and use a heated iron to add liquor to make a potion to be consumed in a cup.

In haste, simply using freshly drawn water to grind ink for consumption may yield unfavorable results. Alternatively, herbs like Xiong, Gui, Yi Mu Cao, and Kui Xin can all help expel stagnation and facilitate childbirth.

For shorter women whose pelvic bones are narrow and difficult childbirth occurs, Gui Ke Powder or Ancient Xiong Gui Decoction may be used. To treat difficult deliveries in general, Worry-Free Powder, Cai Su Powder, and Tu Nao Pills can be used.[37p]
Fetuses that die in the womb, with external signs of dark blue-black nails, bloating and inability to eat, and an extremely foul odor in the mouth, should be treated with Pingwei Powder, adding five coins of nitre, boiled in water and wine for consumption, which will cause the fetus to transform into blood and water and be expelled. For those with a tight pulse, use Dahuang Beiji Pill; alternatively, grind deer antler into powder and brew it with scallions and soybeans for consumption. For a faint pulse, use Yangzheng Dan and a thick decoction of myrrh, prepared into 120 pills. If the blood is dry or there is cold, take Siwu Decoction with Guxiang Pills. For weak qi, administer Cuisheng Wujisan with a pin of musk.

In cases of twins, where one is dead and one is alive, use one cup of crab claw, two liang of licorice, and ten cups of flowing water, boiled down to three cups, strain it, and then add three liang of Ejiao, dividing into two or three doses to take; this can help stabilize the living one and expel the dead one.

To facilitate the expulsion of a dead fetus, use Pilidang or Duoming Pill, apply Shenggao externally to the soles of the feet, and also take labor-inducing medicine; blowing Tongguan Powder into the nose will also facilitate expulsion.[38p]

Pulse Diagnosis

When approaching labor, there are six vital signs, known as the "deviation pulse." If the pulse is deep, fine, and slippery, it indicates impending birth; if the pulse is floating and large, it signifies difficult labor, and if cold and hot sensations are frequent, this is an ominous sign, necessitating urgent observation of the complexion. The cheeks, lips, and tongue should avoid being black or blue. A red face suggests the mother will survive, but the child will be at risk. If the fetus is in the abdomen, both the child and mother may face death.

The "deviation" occurs when the pulse does not follow the usual pattern. In a day and night, the pulse cycles continuously. However, due to the fetus's descent, the gastric pulse deviates from its normal pathway and does not restart from the original cycle, hence the term "deviation." A deep, fine, and slippery pulse indicates the kidney's essence is manifesting; if the pulse is deep but feels absent, it indicates imminent delivery, whereas a floating and large pulse indicates difficulty. If the body feels heavy and hot, and cold and hot sensations occur often, these are ominous signs, requiring urgent examination of the complexion and tongue to ensure the safety of both mother and child. The face reflects the heart's essence, and the tongue reflects the heart's nourishment. A blue complexion suggests liver deficiency unable to store blood, leading to premature rupture of membranes and an inability to move or turn the fetus. A blackish hue indicates kidney water suppressing fire, resulting in both mother and child perishing. Only a red face with a blue tongue indicates that the mother's blood circulates, allowing her survival but leading to the child's demise. If a dead fetus does not exit, the mother's life is also at risk.[39p]

Xue's Medical Case
[Ming Dynasty, Xue Ji]

Preparation of Medicines for the Month of Admission

In the month of admission, one should prepare the following medicines: Buddha's Hand, Baoqi, Zhike, Elm Bark, Heishen, Dasheng, and Huairui Stone Seven Powder, as well as Shenqing, Baosheng, and Lizhong Three Pills, Cuisheng and Heihu Two Elixirs, along with Cuisheng Shenfu. Additionally, prepare Kuiszi, Shengdi Huang, Qianghuo, Zhu Ru, Wumei, Male and Female Shiyan, Gan Cao, Haima, Jujube, Chenpi, Ginger, Qian Hei Dou, and White Honey. Also stock no-ash wine, child urine, sour vinegar, white rice soup, bottles, pots, and scissors for cutting the umbilical cord line.

Among these, Huairui Stone Powder is used for blood entering the fetal membrane, causing it to swell and preventing delivery or for lochia rising and unable to revive. Buddha's Hand Powder treats severe blood deficiency. Jiawei Xionggui Decoction is for difficulties with delivery not opening the bones. Bima Zi treats the fetal membrane unable to move up or down. Shixiao Powder addresses lochia, abdominal pain, and loss of consciousness. Wax oil mixed with talc for application at the birth canal acts as a remedy for smooth delivery. Qinghun Powder treats blood circulation issues. Pingwei Powder, (Shibu) Nitrate, and Mercury are agents for decomposing a stillborn fetus. Ba Zhen Decoction replenishes blood and alleviates energy deficiency.

All the above prescriptions are crucial medicines and must not be omitted. When cutting the umbilical cord, first use a thread to tie it tightly close to the abdomen, then wrap fabric and bite to cut. If the weather is windy and cold, or if the mother and child are laboring with depleted vital energy, first tie the cord and use oiled paper to burn and sever it. This is the essential method for returning life and reviving the dead. Therefore, practitioners must carefully assess the appropriateness of each method and must not blindly trust and apply them.[41p]
Method for Delivery

At the time of impending labor, when one feels the baby moving within the abdomen, one should lie on their back. When the baby turns downward and pain begins, one may try pinching the mother's middle finger; if the middle joint or the base joint pulses, it indicates that labor is imminent.[42p]
Guidelines for Treatment
By Wang Kentang (Ming Dynasty)

Inducing Labor Method
Use smoothness to promote circulation, bitterness to expel stagnation, and fragrance to open the orifices and disperse blood. For those with stagnant qi, move the qi; for those whose vessel walls are exhausted, secure the blood first.

Method for Expelling a Stillborn
For those with cold, use heat to stimulate; for those with heat, use cooling methods; for those who are dry, use moisture to lubricate; for those in acute danger, use toxicity to induce expulsion.

Distinguishing Pulse Patterns
The pulses of women about to give birth depart from the normal pattern, presenting as deep, fine, and slippery. If pain arises at midnight, labor should occur; if pain occurs around noon, birth is imminent. These four lines are often misunderstood. According to the "Pulse Classic," departing from normal means that the pulse is floating; abdominal pain radiating to the lower back signifies labor is approaching. However, a departure from normal does not guarantee childbirth. It also states that if the pulse is departed from at midnight, then birth occurs at midday. The term "normal" refers to its usual state; thus, if a pregnant woman had a deep pulse on the left indicating a male child yesterday, but today the pulse is floating, it is a departure from the usual pulse, differing from yesterday. Moreover, with abdominal pain, it is known that she is about to give birth. "Tong Zhenzi" refers to the "Nanjing," stating that one call results in three occurrences, indicating “departing from normal” as a resolution. Li Xi and Fan further refer to "Nanjing," where one call results in one occurrence, stating “departing from normal” to explain deep, fine, and slippery pulses, but both interpretations are incorrect. "Nanjing" mentions that two occurrences although sharing the name “departing from normal” differ in pulse and principles.[43p]
The Classic on Pulse clearly states that a floating pulse indicates a departure from the regular channels and does not reference the text of the Nan Jing. The Pulse Secrets add that besides being floating, the pulse can also be deep, fine, and slippery. This term "departure from the regular" essentially refers to the pulse of men and women diagnosed before, where it was said that a floating pulse largely indicates a female. If only a floating pulse is interpreted as a departure from the regular, how then can one distinguish between them? Therefore, they also include deep, fine, and slippery to represent that the departure from the regular can be a common floating pulse and is typically slippery. The Holy Compendium states that if one feels abdominal pain at midnight, childbirth will occur by noon the next day. This refers to the conflict between the hour of the Rat and the hour of the Horse, essentially indicating the time of day. The True Essentials say: pain at midnight predicts birth by noon. However, this may not be entirely accurate. It further states that if the abdominal pain does not radiate to the lower back, it indicates no birth yet. In contrast, if the abdominal pain is severe and also affects the lower back, then birth is imminent. This is due to the kidney being connected to the lower back and the uterus being associated with the kidneys. If the pulse at the wrist is turning urgent, like cutting a rope or turning a bead, then childbirth is imminent. Since childbirth can vary in difficulty and the timing of pain can be tight or loose, how can one definitively determine it by mere half days? One should rely on active methods instead.[44p]
Method for Inducing Labor

For women who are in difficulty one or two days before delivery, simply use a modified Wuling Powder. If it has been two or three days, and the woman feels strong and can eat, then it is due to the dryness of the amniotic fluid; use a modified Siwu Decoction to supplement the body's essential fluids. If it has been two or three days, and the woman feels weak with little appetite, this indicates insufficient vital energy, preventing the movement of the fetus; use a modified Sijunzi Decoction in this case. If delivery does not occur after three, four, or five days, or if the fetus has died in utero, then use the Duoming Pill.[45p]

Rescue from Miscarriage

For a child born in a reverse position, one must never use needles to prick the soles of the feet or apply salt, as this will cause the child to experience pain and run about, making the mother’s life difficult to preserve.

Rescue from Obstructed Labor

For obstructed labor, the mother should lie on her back, and the midwife should carefully examine with a light to see where the umbilical cord is entangling the child. The midwife should gently and carefully free it, without haste.

Prolapse of Intestines during Labor

When labor occurs, if the mother’s intestines come out first and are exposed, with the child born afterward, and the intestines do not retract immediately, it is likely due to chronic deficiency of Qi, which cannot constrict. The blood becomes prone to flowing, and the lower source (of vitality) is not secure, hence the instability. To avoid this suffering, one should take more Dong Quai pills supplemented with Schisandra (five-flavor fruit) and cinnamon during non-pregnant periods to strengthen the vital source. When pregnant, one should take more Hu Lian pills with one tael of ginseng to tonify Qi; also, take San Bu pills to cool the blood. Caution is advised with medications that easily lead to miscarriage or weak births. At the time of entering the month, take Ba Wu Decoction with Myrobalan, Flaxseed flower, and honey-fried husk for about ten doses to help prevent this issue.[46p]
The Complete Works of Jingyue by Zhang Jiebin (Ming Dynasty)

Methods for Inducing Labor

When approaching childbirth and experiencing intense abdominal pain, there is no better medicine for inducing labor than the "Tuo Hua Decoction," supplemented with a small amount of cinnamon (five to seven fen) for stability and effectiveness. If there is a deficiency of qi and strength, add two to three qian of ginseng. If the deficiency is severe, one may add it freely. Generally, if the fetus is healthy and the pregnancy lasts the full term, inducing labor is unnecessary; what is called "inducing labor" is merely to assist the blood and qi to facilitate the process. It is advisable to use the Tuo Hua Decoction or the "Hua Tai Decoction" when the time arrives, adjusting based on symptoms. If the mother has been in labor for a long time and feels exhausted, she should take the Hua Tai Decoction to boost her qi and blood, allowing the child to be born quickly. For those with weak qi and strength, making it difficult to deliver, the "Du Shen Tang" is essential, adjusting the amount as needed to support her strength, which is crucial for inducing labor. However, if one uses qi-moving and blood-guiding agents prematurely, thinking they are inducing labor, it is like removing the bud from a flower or pulling the seedling from the soil.[47p]

On Divination and Inquiry Regarding Childbirth

During pregnancy and childbirth, one should not resort to divination or inquire of deities, as those akin to shamans and prophets often deceive for profit, speaking of dangers and misfortunes. When a pregnant woman hears such things, it leads to anxiety and fear. Such worries cause the qi to become stagnant and unyielding, often resulting in difficult labor; thus, it should be avoided.

On Nourishing Qi and Blood During Pregnancy

Before childbirth, clear qi is necessary, and after childbirth, blood must be replenished; however, one should not be overly rigid about this. If the spleen and stomach are weak, and qi and blood are deficient, one must take steps to nourish them in advance; otherwise, there will be many troubles when labor occurs.

On Miscarriage

The approach to preventing miscarriage is solely to ensure that the time of childbirth is both easy and swift. The ease or difficulty stems from the abundance or deficiency of blood, not from medicinal properties aimed at inducing labor. Abundant blood provides moisture, making labor easy, whereas deficiency leads to dryness, making it difficult. Therefore, before labor, one should primarily focus on nourishing qi and blood in preparation. Formulas such as Si Wu Decoction, Miscarriage Prevention Decoction, Five Blessings Drink, Little Nourishment Decoction, and Eight Treasures Soup are essential for preventing miscarriage. Misuse of slippery or stimulating substances, or premature use of harsh herbs to purify heat and move qi when labor is not imminent, can harm the essential qi and deplete true yin, leading to severe deficiencies. If one is robust and full of qi, then formulas such as Zisu Drink, Baosheng Wuyou Powder, and Miscarriage Prevention Zhiqiao Powder can be chosen for use.[48p]

催生柞木饮子
To promote childbirth in cases of difficult labor (whether transverse or breech) and for stillbirths causing abdominal distention, this remedy has proven effective multiple times.

Take a large branch of oak about the size of a hand, one foot long, wash it thoroughly, and shred it. Use five sections of licorice, each five inches long, also shredded.

Combine with three and a half liters of fresh spring water in a new ceramic bottle, sealing it tightly with three layers of paper. Do not take it if she does not have heavy pain in her waist. If she feels thirsty, she may take another cup, up to three or four, until she feels heaviness below, at which point she will give birth. This remedy is the most effective.

Xingqi Cuisheng Decoction

This is used for a difficult labor during pregnancy when contractions are still sparse, and after two or three days without delivery, resulting in fetal demise in the womb. It is also suitable for mothers who are weak and exhausted, with a dry birth canal. When strong pains are felt after the water has broken, it can be taken.

Ingredients:

  • 2 taels of Cangzhu, soaked and fried in rice wash
  • Gehao (thick jujube peel) without the pith, fried
  • Jie geng (Platycodon root)
  • Chen pi (dried tangerine peel) without the white part
  • Shao yao (peony root)
  • Bai zhi (angelica)
  • Chuan xiong (Sichuan lovage)
  • Gui wei (ligusticum)
  • Ban xia (pinellia), washed
  • Gui (cinnamon) without the coarse skin and not exposed to fire
  • Fen cao (glossy ganoderma)
  • Ma huang (ephedra) without joints
  • Jun jiang (ginger) peeled
  • Hou po (magnolia bark) without coarse skin and fried with ginger juice
  • Bai fu ling (white poria)
  • Nan mu xiang (sandalwood) not exposed to fire
  • Xing ren (apricot kernel), peeled and ground separately, each 5 qian (money)

These are ground into a powder, and 2 qian of it is taken with warm water. If there is heat and congestion, use white honey tea. Alternatively, it can be chopped and simmered with a cup of true rice vinegar.

In this formula, Shao yao and rou gui aid in opening the uterus, while the other herbs support the qi. When the yang qi is strong, blood circulates, leading to childbirth. It dispels cold pathogens and alleviates accumulation, making it particularly effective in cold months, while caution is advised in hot, humid weather. In such cases, Wuling San with light boiling water should be used to clear heat and promote easy labor.

If the amniotic sac has ruptured, leading to difficulty in delivery, soak white honey in hot wine to help with delivery.

The modified Chuan Gui decoction, also known as Turtle Shell Powder, is for obstructed delivery, unable to give birth, or for women nearing death from prolonged labor. One tael each of Chuanxiong and Danggui, and one piece of a dead turtle’s shell, prepared with oil. For women with abundant hair, use a fistful, burned to preserve its essence. This is made into a powder; each dose is five qian, decocted in water for consumption. After walking about five li, childbirth will occur. It can also expel a dead fetus. Make sure the turtle shell is properly burned first.[64p]
Wujin San

This is for treating difficult childbirth and fevers, where the fetus has died in the womb, possibly due to falls, drops from heights, or early agitation during childbirth, violating taboos, or other circumstances. Sometimes, the blood may come down too early before labor, and if the lochia has ceased, it can lead to a dead fetus with a cold body and inability to emerge. The signs include a red face and a blue tongue in the mother. If the face is blue and the tongue red, the mother is dead while the child lives. If there is a blue lip with foam, both mother and child are dead. There may also be twins where one dies while the other lives, and the signs can be difficult to determine; one must observe changes at the moment.

Ingredients:

  • Cooked Rehmannia Root, washed, sliced, dried, and roasted in wine
  • Real Cyperus Rhizome
  • Angelica Sinensis
  • Cassia from Jiaozhi
  • Peony Root
  • Ginger (peeled)
  • Sweet Flag (Acorus)
  • Black Soybeans (4 taels)
  • Baicao Frost (5 qian)

Grind everything into a powder. Each dose is 2 qian, mixed with half a cup of rice vinegar, and 6-7 parts of boiling water for warm consumption. If there is uncertainty about the condition, first take Fo Shou Powder with wine; boil and drink 2-3 doses to check. If not dead, both mother and child will be fine; if the fetus has died, it will be expelled. If it is known that the fetus is dead, take this medicine, then follow with Xianggui Powder shortly after, as if pushing it out with the hand.

For regular use to induce labor, also add half a tael of Talc Powder, 50 shredded sunflower seeds, 7-8 pieces of crushed oak leaves, and 2 inches of green onion, boiled in water to make a decoction. Talc benefits urination, oak leaves promote qi and remove blood, while green onion communicates the yang energy within. When the qi is vigorous and blood flows, labor will occur.[65p]
Formula for Treating Stillbirths: For a pregnancy of three to five months with the fetus dead in utero without expulsion.

Ingredients:

  • Large abdominal child (an herb)
  • Red Peony (3 taels)
  • Elm bark (3 taels)
  • Angelica (1 tael, to be fried)
  • Talcum powder (7.5 qian)
  • Jube (a herb)
  • Fried sunflower seeds (half a tael)
  • Poria (half a tael)
  • Powdered herb (half a tael)
  • Root of Scutellaria (half a tael)

Preparation: Grind the above ingredients into a coarse powder. For each dose, take 4 qian, mix with 1 cup of water, and boil until reduced by two-thirds. Strain and consume warm at any time.

Another Formula: For a fetus dead in the abdomen, either not yet expelled halfway or partially lodged in the spine, which causes lack of production, where the blood and qi disturb the mother's heart, resulting in loss of color, faintness, and a feeling of impending death.

Ingredients:

  • Pig fat (1 jin)
  • White honey (1 sheng)
  • Strong wine (2 sheng)[66p]
    Combine the three ingredients and decoct them. Take two sheng, divide into two doses, if unable to drink, take as much as one can manage.

This remedy, "God's Powder," treats retained dead fetuses and broken membranes without birth. This formula has repeatedly proven effective, saving countless lives. The yellow ghost plant, regardless of the amount, is to be processed into a fine powder, as fine as flour, without sifting, pinched between the fingers. For each dose, take three qian of this powder, mix with a cup of unslaked wine, decoct until reduced to one-eighth, then take orally for immediate effect.

Another formula treats difficult labor and retained dead fetuses, especially in critical situations during delivery. One whole snake skin is burned and ground over a lamp, along with a small amount of musk. This is ground to a powder, mixed with equal parts of child's urine and wine; taking one dose will produce immediate effects.

"Rabbit Brain Pills" [from "Entering the Door"] treat difficult labor with prolonged blood loss.

Use the following ingredients: rabbit brain marrow from December, one part male rat kidney, one qian each of mother corydalis and motherwort, two and a half qian of frankincense, and two and a half fen of musk. Grind these into a powder, form into pills the size of coix seeds, coat with cinnabar, wrap in oiled paper, and阴干 (air dry). For each pill, take with vinegar soup to induce labor. Males will emerge with left fists, females with right fists.[67p]
Xiao Ying Jian (Small Decoction)
For the afterbirth not being expelled, taking this during the month of confinement facilitates birth easily.
Ingredients:

  • Angelica (Dang Gui)
  • White Peony (Bai Shao) roasted
  • Chinese Yam (Shan Yao)
  • Goji Berries (Gou Qi Zi) - each 2 qian
  • Honey-fried Licorice (Zhi Gan Cao) - 1 qian
  • Prepared Rehmannia (Shu Di) - 2 to 3 qian
  • Water - 2 sheng
    Preparation: Boil down to 7 parts, take warm after meals.

Tuo Hua Jian (Flower Expulsion Decoction)
For those about to give birth, it is best to take this medicine first to promote labor. It is also effective for difficult labor lasting several days, or if stillbirth does not descend.
Ingredients:

  • Angelica (Dang Gui) - 7 to 8 qian or 1 liang
  • Cinnamon (Rou Gui) - 1 to 3 qian
  • Chuan Xiong (Chuan Xiong)
  • Cowherb (Niu Xi) - each 2 qian
  • Plantago Seed (Che Qian Zi) - 0.5 qian
  • Safflower (Hong Hua) - 1 qian, used to promote birth, can omit
  • Water - 2 sheng
    Preparation: Boil down to 8 parts and take warm. Drinking a few cups of wine afterward is also effective. If the fetus has died in the womb or is not descending, add 3 to 5 qian of nitrated sodium.
